 CONDITIONS OF ADMISSION AND 
AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Norton Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Norton Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as
indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________

V. ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS:
I agree to the assignment of all third-party benefits to the facility and agree to pay the facility for all charges not covered by third-party payors. In the case of outpatient services I agree that this
document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically revoked by me in writing. Any sums not paid by a third-party payor are my obligation.
VI. RELEASE OF INSURANCE INFORMATION TO FACILITY:
I agree to the release by my insurance carrier to the facility and the facility's billing service of any eligibility and utilization data concerning my insurance coverage which the facility and/or its billing 
supplier may require. I authorize the facility to file an appeal of a payment denial and/or request a hearing regarding any denial of payment for treatment provided to me. I further authorize the facility 
to present proof, utilize facility records and my records and documentation for appeals and hearings.
VII. PAYMENT OF FACILITY BILLS WHEN DUE:
I am liable for the payment of the account of the facility and I am obligated to pay the account of the facility, in accordance with the regular rates and terms of the facility. If my injury is work-related, I am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of
bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an
attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the
attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the status and collection of 
my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded voice systems.

XI. PATIENT BILL OF RIGHTS: I acknowledge that a copy of the Patient Bill of Rights has been made available to me.

[DOB-402] - Admission (Discharged) in NH 4K (continued)
OP Notes (continued)
ASSISTANT: Tina Woodson. DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: The patient was placed in the supine position with the neck slightly
hyperextended. The anterior aspect of the neck was shaved, prepped and draped in the usual fashion. An
incision was outlined in the upper aspect of the cervical spine on the right side. A cross-table cervical spine
x-ray was taken with a lumbar puncture marker. Once the localizing x-ray was taken, the incision was
opened and dissection carried deeply to the platysma. The platysma was sectioned longitudinally and
separated from overlying and underlying tissue. The anterior aspect of the neck was approached with the
trachea and esophagus reflected medially and the carotid sheath laterally. The correct level was identified
by a cross-table cervical spine x-ray. The annulus of the disc was incised and removed, and cartilaginous
endplate and soft disc tissue were removed from the disc space at C3-4. The disc space spreader was
inserted and then allowed to move under the posterior aspect of the disc at C3-4 along with a bony spur
projecting posteriorly from the lower aspect of the C3 vertebral body and the upper aspect of the C4
vertebral body. The dural tube was identified and wide foraminotomies were performed on both sides. That
resulted in excellent decompression of the C4 nerve root. The surfaces of C3 and C4 were made parallel
using a 6 mm rasp. A 6 mm PEEK cage filled with bone chips and VIA graft was inserted into the disc space
at C3-4 and countersunk approximately 2 mm. The entire area was irrigated through copiously with
Bacitracin solution and saline and hemostasis was secured. At that point, Dr. John Johnson of the
orthopedic spine service entered the operating room to proceed with placement of cervical plate. Tina Woodson was first assistant during this operation and she greatly facilitated this performance with
control of blood loss and muscle retraction. Christopher B. Shields, MD
D: [DOB-401] 10:23:33
T: [DOB-400] 10:46:00/MODL

PROCEDURE PERFORMED: Anterior Anodyne cervical stabilizing plate, C3-C4. PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Herniated nucleus pulposus, C3 to C4. POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Herniated nucleus pulposus, C3 to C4. FIRST ASSISTANT: Kristi Turner, APRN 
Kristi was present during the instrumentation and closure of the wound. PROCEDURE: After the patient had undergone a C3-4 discectomy and bone grafting by Dr. Christopher
Shields, which will be dictated as a separate procedure, the procedure was then turned over to the
orthopedic spine team. Using a caliper, a 13 mm in length Anodyne cervical stabilizing plate was sized to fit across from C3 to C4
and was transfixed to the vertebral body with 12 mm self-tapping screws, 2 into the vertebral body of C3 and
2 into the vertebral body of C4. All screws at the time of surgery had firm fixation by fill in bone. Lateral xray was taken to verify position of the plate, bone graft, and screws. One screw appeared to be slightly
lower on the lateral at C3 level; however, it still appeared to be above the marker of the cage at the superior
portion of C3. Because of the fact that it had good fixation in bone by fill, 2 x-rays were taken. Still, the
position seemed to be a little bit inferior on the x-rays, but the cervical spine appeared to be somewhat
oblique, and it was felt, because of the good fixation, that we would accept this. The wound was then closed
in layers, sterile dressing was applied, and the patient was taken to the recovery room for further
postoperative care. John Johnson, MD

Know how to care for your wound. Emphasize good hand hygiene before and after caring for the the wound. Teach about signs and symptoms of infection and when to notify healthcare provider. Teach to tell family and friends to never touch wound or bandage and to clean their hands before and after visiting.
Instruct to keep incision/wound as clean and dry as possible. Caution against: scrubbing or rubbing the incision, removing the tape strips, using lotion or powder around the incision, exposing the incision to sunlight, taking a bath unless the incision can be kept dry. Point: Bandage/Dressing Care (Done)
Encourage the patient/family/caregiver to ask any questions about bandage/dressing care. Point: Incision Support (Done)
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver that patient may get puffy and look swollen. Need to reposition frequently, elevate
extremities above heart level if possible, use ice packs as ordered, maintain fluid and diet control. Learning Progress Summary
Description:

Learning Progress Summary
Description:

keep bandage/dressing clean and dry as possible. Caution against: using lots of tape, using lotion or powder around
bandage, getting bandage/dressing wet when taking a bath or shower. Emphasize good hand hygiene. If patient is not to
change bandage/dressing, instruct him/her to make follow-up appointment with healthcare provider to have
bandage/dressing changed. Learning Progress Summary

Description:

pain.
Patient Friendly Description: -Your nurse will ask you to rate our pain on a scale of zero (0), for no pain, to ten (10), the
worst pain you can experience. -Your nurse will ask you to set a pain goal within zero (0) to ten (10) so that he or she can be sure that what we are doing
is working. -Mild pain is 1-3, Moderate pain is 4-6 and severe pain is 7-10. -We may not be able to take away ALL pain, so try to identify a point that pain would be manageable. -So if your pain goal is 4 or less and you are rating your pain at 7, your nurse would give you a pain medication and then
re-check your pain to ensure it is moving toward your pain goal of 4. Learning Progress Summary

[DOB-304] - Admission (Discharged) in NH 4K (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Topic: Infection Prevention (In Progress)
Point: Discuss that Pain Control is Important Part of Treatment (Done)
Point: Let Staff Know if Patient is Having Any Pain (Done)
Point: Multi-drug Resistant Organism (Done)
Explain that an MDRO is a strain of bacteria that is resistant to common antibiotics used to treat infections. Infections can
vary, depending on the organism. MDROs can cause skin infections (boils, abscesses), urinary tract infections, blood stream
infections, and pneumonia, and they can infect wounds, the respiratory tract and surgical sites. Point: Protect Others from Infection (Done)
Point: Protect Yourself from Further Infection (Done)
Description:
Explain to patient/family/caregiver that there are other ways of controlling pain than medication. The following are
suggestions: position change, aromatherapy, deep slow breathing, distraction, quiet environment, imagery, heat therapy
and/or cold therapy, laughter, massage, music, physical therapy, and touch therapy. Learning Progress Summary
Learning Progress Summary
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver about healthcare associate infection prevention strategies. Teach hand hygiene and
wearing of gloves, gowns and mask when appropriate. Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate on respiratory hygiene and cough etiquette. To protect from further infection and to protect others from getting an
infection, patient should cover nose and mouth with tissues when coughing. Encourage patient to place used tissues in a
plastic bag that will not allow secretions to soak through. Patient should always wash their hands after using or handling
used tissues.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate that because patient is in a weakened condition he/she needs to avoid others who are sick as to not acquire
another illness; should wear gloves, gown and face shield/eye protection.

[DOB-312] - Admission (Discharged) in NH 4K (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Title: First-Dose Education ()
Topic: Anticoagulant Therapy (In Progress)
Points For This Title
Point: Lab Tests (Specify) (Done)
Point: Radiology Tests (Specify) (Done)
Point: Blood Transfusion (Done)
In a blood transfusion, donated blood is added to patient's own blood. A blood transfusion may also be done to supplement
various components of the patient's blood with donated blood products. During a typical blood transfusion, certain parts of blood are delivered through an intravenous (IV) line that's placed in the
patient. A blood transfusion usually takes two to four hours, though in an emergency it can be done much faster. A blood transfusion boosts blood levels that are low, either because the body isn't making enough or because blood has been
lost during surgery, injury or disease
Point: Sequential Compression Device (Done)
Point: ceFAZolin Sodium (Done)

 CONDITIONS OF ADMISSION AND 
AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Norton Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Norton Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or

[DOB-388] - Admission (Discharged) in NH PAV Periop Services (continued)
OP Notes (continued)
Preoperative Antibiotics: Kefzol
Complications: None
Drains: none
Specimens: None
Estimated blood loss: 5 mL
Description of Procedure: Patient was met in the preoperative area the
operative extremity was identified and marked. They were then brought to the
operative suite. After the satisfactory induction of general anesthesia,the 
operative extremity was prepped and draped in a normal sterile manner. Surgical time-out was then called to confirm that the patient had been given
appropriate preoperative antibiotics, that this was the correct patient, correct
procedure, and correct operative extremity. 
A posterior portal was established in the glenohumeral joint was entered. An
anterior portal was established.
The underside of the rotator cuff is intact. The articular cartilage of the
glenohumeral joint was intact. As predicted on the MRI there was a discrete
anterior attachment of the labrum at the 9 o'clock position. The bicep tendon and
anchor were intact. An arthroscopic Freer was used to dissect the area of the
tear and then a rasp was used to abrade the anterior bony glenoid. The labrum was then reapproximated using a single bioabsorbable suture
anchor.
An accessory superior lateral portal was established and scope was placed in the
subacromial space. A complete subacromial bursectomy was performed and
then the shaver was used to remove the underlying acromial spur. The top side
of the rotator cuff was intact
All fluid and soft tissue debris was drained from the joint. The portals were closed
with nylon, and covered with a dry sterile dressing.

Procedures
Clinical Notes
PATIENT INSTRUCTIONS
POST-ANESTHESIA
IMMEDIATELY FOLLOWING SURGERY: Do not drive, drink any alcohol, operate machinery, make important
decisions, or sign any legal paperwork for the next twenty four hours after surgery or while taking narcotic pain
medications or sedatives. You may experience a sore throat, mild nausea, dizziness, drowsiness, or a headache. These symptoms are normal after surgery and will subside in the next 24 hours. If you develop severe nausea and
vomiting, a severe headache, or a high fever please notify your doctor immediately.

Patient Education (continued)
Point: Special Care Needs Related to Specific Surgery (Specify in Comments or Add Teaching Point) (Resolved)
Point: Incision/Wound Care (Resolved)
Know how to care for your wound. Emphasize good hand hygiene before and after caring for the the wound. Teach about signs and symptoms of infection and when to notify healthcare provider. Teach to tell family and friends to never touch wound or bandage and to clean their hands before and after visiting.
Instruct to keep incision/wound as clean and dry as possible. Caution against: scrubbing or rubbing the incision, removing the tape strips, using lotion or powder around the incision, exposing the incision to sunlight, taking a bath unless the incision can be kept dry.
Point: Bandage/Dressing Care (Resolved)
Encourage the patient/family/caregiver to ask any questions about bandage/dressing care.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on the specific care needs, reason, how to perform and expected length of time needed
due to surgery.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on how to care for incision/wound to include: how to clean, when to clean and any special
instruction for cleaning.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on how to care for bandage/dressing to include: how to change, when to change and any
special instruction for changing. Demonstrate changing a bandage/dressing and receive a return demonstation. Teach to
keep bandage/dressing clean and dry as possible. Caution against: using lots of tape, using lotion or powder around
bandage, getting bandage/dressing wet when taking a bath or shower. Emphasize good hand hygiene. If patient is not to
change bandage/dressing, instruct him/her to make follow-up appointment with healthcare provider to have
bandage/dressing changed.

AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Norton Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Norton Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as
indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________
